        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.9b14366"><meta property="og:title" content="Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/acsami.9b14366.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Herein, a metal–organic framework (MOF)/polythiophene (PTh)-derived S-doped carbon is successfully designed and prepared employing zeolitic imidazolate frameworks (ZIF-8/ZIF-67) and thiophene (Th) as precursors. The S-doped carbon presents a neuronlike three-dimensional network structure (3DSC). The 3DSC delivers extra-high capacities (225 mAh/g at 5000 mA/g after 3000 cycles) and excellent endurance ability of current changes when applied in Na-ion batteries (SIBs). Moreover, when the 3DSC-700 anode is coupled with a sodium vanadium phosphate cathode to construct a Na-ion full cell, after 50 cycles, a high capacity of ∼229.64 mAh/g is obtained at 100 mA/g. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy analysis, density functional theory calculations, and pseudocapacitance contributions are adopted to investigate the excellent sodium storage mechanism of the 3DSC electrode. A new idea has been provided in this work to open up the possibility of MOF materials and carbon-based materials applications in SIBs in the future."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/acsami.9b14366.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6ec7b0c6e775c-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6ec7b0c6e775c-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '89f29ea2-f512-4500-8b0b-aa3b201831f3'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6ec7b0c6e775c-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

.show-recommended__wrapper .sponsoredContent { display: none; }

data-getftr-references-enabled="data-getFTR-references-enabled" data-getftr-reference-url="/action/CitationEntitlement" data-getftr-citedby-enabled="data-getFTR-citedBy-enabled" <script nonce="90f6ec7b0c6e775c-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Metal–Organic Framework/Polythiophene Derivative: Neuronlike S-Doped Carbon 3D Structure with Outstanding Sodium Storage Performance", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b14366", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/medium/am9b14366_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b14366&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Herein, a metal–organic framework (MOF)/polythiophene (PTh)-derived S-doped carbon is successfully designed and prepared employing zeolitic imidazolate frameworks (ZIF-8/ZIF-67) and thiophene (Th) as precursors. The S-doped carbon presents a neuronlike three-dimensional network structure (3DSC). The 3DSC delivers extra-high capacities (225 mAh/g at 5000 mA/g after 3000 cycles) and excellent endurance ability of current changes when applied in Na-ion batteries (SIBs). Moreover, when the 3DSC-700 anode is coupled with a sodium vanadium phosphate cathode to construct a Na-ion full cell, after 50 cycles, a high capacity of ∼229.64 mAh/g is obtained at 100 mA/g. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy analysis, density functional theory calculations, and pseudocapacitance contributions are adopted to investigate the excellent sodium storage mechanism of the 3DSC electrode. A new idea has been provided in this work to open up the possibility of MOF materials and carbon-based materials applications in SIBs in the future.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D37850%26pageCount%3D9%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DWen%2BZhong%252C%2BXingshuai%2BLv%252C%2BQianwu%2BChen%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D11%26issueNum%3D41%26contentID%3Dacsami.9b14366%26title%3DMetal%25E2%2580%2593Organic%2BFramework%252FPolythiophene%2BDerivative%253A%2BNeuronlike%2BS-Doped%2BCarbon%2B3D%2BStructure%2Bwith%2BOutstanding%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BPerformance%26numPages%3D9%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D37858%26publicationDate%3DOctober%2B2019" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2019 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries" structure" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Chemical%20structure" class="article__tags__link">Chemical structure</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Materials" article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=S-doped+Carbon&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_S-doped%20carbon">S-doped carbon</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Metal%E2%88%92organic+Frameworks&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_metal%E2%88%92organic%20frameworks">metal−organic frameworks</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Pseudocapacitance&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_pseudocapacitance">pseudocapacitance</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Density+Functional+Theory+Calculations&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_density%20functional%20theory%20%28DFT%29%20calculations">density functional theory (DFT) calculations</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Nowadays, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) with good cycling stability and high capacity have been widely utilized in electromobile devices, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> while an uneven geological distribution and limited lithium compel people to look for new energy storage substitutes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3 ref4'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 3 and 4">(3,4)</a> In recent years, owing to the cost-efficiency, rich resources, and analogous chemical properties to Li, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 5 and 6">(5,6)</a> Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as substitutes for LIBs. However, due to the larger Na<sup>+</sup>, a majority of materials do not have sufficiently big space to host it; <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4 ref7'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref7" aria-label="reference 4 and 7">(4,7)</a> thus, compared with LIBs, the development process of SIBs is quite sluggish. Therefore, finding suitable SIB electrode materials is a key factor in developing SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8 ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 8 and 9">(8,9)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Thus far, a variety of materials like metal alloys, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a> metal oxide/sulfide/phosphide, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11 ref12'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 11 and 12">(11,12)</a> etc. were studied as anode materials for SIBs, while carbon-based materials with good structural stability, abundant resource, cost-efficiency, and nontoxicity are regarded as the most promising anodes for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13 ref14 ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 13 to 15">(13−15)</a> However, due to the smaller layer spacing of carbon and larger Na<sup>+</sup>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8" aria-label="reference 8">(8)</a> the most mature carbon-based anodes for LIBs are unsuitable for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16 ref17 ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17 ref18" aria-label="reference 16 to 18">(16−18)</a> Zhou et al. and other researchers through calculation and experimental methods testified that heteroatom doping especially larger size atom doping can enhance the electric conductivity and enlarge the layer spacing of carbon. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15 ref19 ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref19 ref20" aria-label="reference 15, 19 and 20">(15,19,20)</a> Until now, a lot of heteroatom-doped particularly N-doped carbon were investigated as anodes for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21 ref22 ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 21 to 23">(21−23)</a> However, due to the complicated preparation processes, compared to N-doped, studies about S- or P-doped carbon are rare.</div><div class="NLM_p">Moreover, recently metal–organic frameworks (MOFs) have attracted widespread attention due to their attractive characteristics, such as regular structures and high surface areas and porosities. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27" aria-label="reference 24 to 27">(24−27)</a> For the reason that MOF-derived materials can inherit the excellent properties of MOFs, numerous MOF-derived materials have been prepared and applied in many fields. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref29 ref30 ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref29 ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 28 to 31">(28−31)</a> Recently, MOF-derived materials also were investigated as anodes for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref33 ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33 ref34" aria-label="reference 32 to 34">(32−34)</a> However, due to the serious structural collapse, these materials always exhibit poor cycling stability and rate performance when applied in SIBs, even if they have special initial structures or high theoretical specific capacities. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a> Therefore, borrowing the special properties of MOFs and designing new MOF-derived materials with stable structure and excellent sodium storage performance are challenges for MOFs.</div><div class="NLM_p last">To overcome the above defects, a neuronlike three-dimensional (3D) network structure carbon with S-doping and metal particle decoration was fabricated via in situ polymerization using Th and pre-prepared ZIF-8/ZIF-67 as precursors. The neuronlike 3D structure, sulfur doping, and metal particle decoration endow the three-dimensional network structure (3DSC) electrode with excellent extra-long cycling stability at 5000 mA/g (225 mAh/g after 3000 cycles).</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4"> Materials Synthesis</h3><div id="sec2_1_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_3"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h4 class="article-section__title" id="_i5"> Preparation of the ZIF-8/ZIF-67 Precursor</h4><div class="NLM_p last">First, Zn (NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O (1.62 g) methanol solutions and 2-methylimidazole (1.11 g) methanol solution were mixed and kept under magnetic stirring for 12 h. Then, the ZIF-8 precipitate was collected through centrifugation, washed with pure methanol solution, and dried at 80 °C for 12 h. Second, 0.16 g of ZIF-8 was added into 20 mL of methanol solution with vigorous ultrasonication for 30 min, then magnetic stirring for 20 min. Then, the ZIF-8, CoCl<sub>2</sub> (0.35 g), and 2-methylimidazole (1.79) methanol solutions were mixed and magnetically stirred for 5 min. Finally, the mixture was transferred into an autoclave (50 mL) and kept at 100 °C for 12 h. The ZIF-8/ZIF-67 precursor was collected through the same process as that of ZIF-8.</div></div><div id="sec2_1_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_3"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h4 class="article-section__title" id="_i6"> Preparation of the ZIF-8/ZIF-67/PTh 3D Network Intermediate and 3DSC-700</h4><div class="NLM_p last">First, the ZIF-8/ZIF-67 precursor (0.16 g), 155 μL of Th trichloromethane solutions, and FeCl<sub>3</sub> (1.25 g) trichloromethane solutions were mixed and ultrasonicated for 50 min. Then, the mixture was poured into a three-necked flask (250 mL) and kept at 65 °C for 4 h with mechanical stirring. Second, to remove the iron ions, 100 mL of methanol was poured into the flask and continued to react for 24 h at 65 °C. Finally, the ZIF-8/ZIF-67/PTh 3D network intermediate was obtained through the same process as that of ZIF-8. The prepared ZIF-8/ZIF-67/PTh intermediate was treated at 700 °C under an argon atmosphere for 3 h to obtain 3DSC-700 (700 represents the annealing temperature). ZIF-8/ZIF-67-derived carbon (MDC-700) and PTh-derived S-doped C (SC-700) were fabricated through the analogous procedure except for the reaction with thiophene and ZIF-8/ZIF-67, respectively. Meanwhile, ZIF-67/PTh-derived carbon (67/SC-700) and ZIF-8/PTh-derived carbon (8/SC-700) were prepared through a similar procedure.</div></div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7"> Material Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The as-prepared materials were studied by an X-ray Diffractometer using Cu Kα radiation (Shimadzu XRD-6100AS). Nitrogen adsorption isotherms and Brunauer–Emmett–Teller surface area were investigated by a Micromeritcs GeminiV2380 analyzer operating at 77 K. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) analysis was conducted using an ESCALAB 250 spectrometer with Mg Kα radiation as the excitation source. Morphological characterization of the synthesized materials was done using a Tecnai G<sup>2</sup>F30 S-Twin transmission electron microscope (TEM), Hitachi S-4800 scanning electron microscope (SEM), and high-resolution TEM (HRTEM, Tecnai G<sup>2</sup>F30 S-Twin). Elemental distributions of the products were observed using Tecnai G<sup>2</sup>F30 S-Twin energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS).</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8"> Electrochemical Tests</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Sodium storage performances of the synthesized materials were tested in standard CR2032 simulated batteries. Test electrodes were manufactured through the same procedure we reported in ref  <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a>. The electrolyte and separator used in this work were the same as those reported in ref  <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a>. Charge/discharge tests were conducted on LAHE battery test systems at 25 °C (potential range 0.01–3.0 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). A CHI760E electrochemical workstation was used to test the cyclic voltammograms (CVs) and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS). The diameter of each circular electrode was 12 mm, and the average active material mass per unit area of the used electrode was about ∼0.7 mg/cm<sup>2</sup>. In the Na-ion full cells, the 3DSC-700 anode was coupled with a homemade sodium vanadium phosphate (NVP) cathode and the weight ratio of the anode/cathode was 1/4.09.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p"><a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="Scheme 1">Scheme </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="1">1</a> illustrates the preparation process and electron transport mechanism of 3DSC-700. The ZIF-8/ZIF-67 dodecahedron was synthesized first, and then the ZIF-8/ZIF-67/PTh intermediate was prepared through an in situ polymerization reaction. During the polymerization reaction of thiophene, the thiophene monomer first self-polymerized to form long PTh nanofibers and then the long PTh nanofibers were assembled into a neuronlike 3D network structure using the ZIF-8/ZIF-67 dodecahedron as a fulcrum. Finally, a neuronlike 3D ZIF-8/ZIF-67/PTh intermediate formed after the polymerization reaction. During the subsequent calcination process, the ZIF-8/ZIF-67/PTh intermediate changed into a neuronlike 3D carbon network and the sulfur in PTh can homogeneously dope into the carbon lattice. As can be seen in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="Scheme 1">Scheme </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="1">1</a>, the electrons in this material, like neural induction, can transmit quickly in the entire 3D structure during the electrochemical process.</div><figure id="sch1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Scheme 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/medium/am9b14366_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0007.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><div class="title2">Scheme 1. Schematic of the Preparation Procedure of 3DSC-700</div></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b14366&amp;id=sch1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a shows the X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns of 3DSC-700, SC-700, and MDC-700. A broad peak at ∼23° appears in all of the three samples, which represents the (002) plane of amorphous carbon. Moreover, the calculated d-spacing values of MDC-700, SC-700, and 3DSC-700 based on the XRD results using Bragg’s equation are 0.362, 0.381, and 0.395 nm, respectively. This result confirms that sulfur doping could effectively expand the interlayer spacing of carbon materials. The most difference between the three samples is that there are other three intense diffraction peaks in the MDC-700 XRD pattern, which corresponds to Co metal (JCPDS No. 15-0806), and the Co comes from ZIF-67. There are two wide peaks centered at around 1350 and 1587 cm<sup>–1</sup> in Raman spectra of the 3DSC-700, SC-700, and MDC-700 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b), which are assigned to carbon’s D band and G band. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> The D band and G band reflect the defective structure and graphitic structure in carbon. The intensity ratio of D and G values of 3DSC-700 is ∼0.99, illustrating the higher graphitization degree in 3DSC-700, which is helpful for electronic transmission. The nitrogen adsorption–desorption isotherm in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c indicates that the isotherm of 3DSC-700 is type IV, and the hysteresis loop suggests the mesoporous architecture of 3DSC-700. Due to its special architecture, 3DSC-700 presents a higher specific surface area of 419 m<sup>2</sup>/g. 3DSC-700 presents microporous and mesoporous architectures, which can be seen in the pore-size distribution profile (inset in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c). XPS was conducted to identify the elemental composition of 3DSC-700. The XPS spectrum of 3DSC-700 shows that the sample contains C, S, N, Co, and Zn elements (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2a</a>). N, Co, and Zn come from the ZIF-8/ZIF-67 precursor. There are four fitted peaks located at 286.4, 284.9, 284.5, and 284.1 eV in the C 1s spectrum (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2b</a>), which are ascribed to C–N groups, C–S, C–C, and C═C respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref38 ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 12, 38 and 39">(12,38,39)</a> The two fitted peaks at 165.0 and 163.8 eV in the S 2p spectrum (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>d) corresponds to S 2p<sub>1/2</sub> and S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> for the thiophene-type −C–S–C– bond. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> The S content in the 3DSC-700 is as high as 20.1 wt % (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>) according to the elemental analysis results. The absorption peak at 1119 cm<sup>–1</sup> in the 3DSC-700 Fourier transform infrared (FTIR) spectrum corresponds to the band of C–S–C (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2c</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> The XPS and FTIR (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2c</a>) results confirm that the S exits in the form of covalent bonds in the carbon lattice, that’s why the S has not been seen in the XRD pattern.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/medium/am9b14366_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0001.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) XRD and (b) Raman spectrum of 3DSC-700, SC-700, and MDC-700, (c) nitrogen adsorption–desorption isotherms, and (d) S 2p XPS spectrum of 3DSC-700.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b14366&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Morphologies and sizes of MDC-700, SC-700, and 3DSC-700 were studied by SEM and TEM. The MDC-700 shows a regular morphology of rhombic dodecahedra with the diameter ranging from 400 to 600 nm, and the little particles on the MDC-700 surface are metal particles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S3</a>). The SC-700 from PTh exhibits a nanofiber morphology, and the nanofibers piled up together (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c,d clearly reveal that the morphology of 3DSC-700 is a neuronlike 3D network structure. There are many polyhedrons scattered in the 3D network in the low-resolution SEM image (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c), which are MOF-derived dodecahedrons and can be distinctly seen in the high-resolution SEM graphics (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d). Due to the PTh coating, the morphology of the dodecahedron becomes irregular. TEM observations also certify the 3D network structure, and the curved line in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a is the PTh-derived carbon. A regular fringe of the MOF-derived dodecahedrons can be apparently detected from the HRTEM image (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b). An obvious interplanar spacing of 2.05 Å corresponds to the Co(111) crystal plane (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c–h present the high-angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (HAADF-STEM) and elemental mappings of the 3DSC-700. EDS elemental mappings exhibit the uniform distribution of carbon (d), sulfur (e), nitrogen (f), cobalt (g), and zinc (h), which shows the same results as XPS.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/medium/am9b14366_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0002.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. SEM of (a) MDC-700, (b) SC-700, (c, d) 3DSC-700.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b14366&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure id="fig3" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/medium/am9b14366_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0003.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) TEM, (b) HRTEM, (c) HAADF-STEM, and (d–h) EDS elemental mapping of 3DSC-700.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b14366&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Sodium storage performances of the 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700 electrodes were evaluated in half coin cells. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S4a, and S5a</a> display the CV curves of the 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700. All of them present a broad peak located at 1.0–1.3 V during the first scan, which can be attributed to the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) formation and irreversible reactions on the electrode surface. The reduction peak close to 0 V is attributed to the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> into the layer of carbon. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42 ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42 ref43" aria-label="reference 42 and 43">(42,43)</a> For the MDC-700 electrode, the reduction peaks located at 1.2, 0.6, 0.28, and 0 V in the initial scan can be ascribed to the irreversible reactions on the MDC-700 surface, the SEI formation, and the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> in the MDC-700 interlayer, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4a</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44 ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44 ref45" aria-label="reference 44 and 45">(44,45)</a> The oxidation peak at 0.85 V in the MDC-700 electrode is mostly related to the reversible reaction between N functional groups and Na<sup>+</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44" aria-label="reference 44">(44)</a> Compared with MDC-700, both 3DSC-700 and SC-700 electrodes exhibit other two pairs of redox peaks centered at 1.15/1.80 and 1.75/2.15 V, which are similar to room-temperature Na–S batteries, and these two pairs of redox peaks are attributed to the Faradaic reactions between covalent sulfur and Na<sup>+</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43 ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43 ref46" aria-label="reference 43 and 46">(43,46)</a> The two pairs of peaks still exist after three cycles, suggesting the electrochemical activity of the covalent sulfur and the highly reversible reaction between S and Na. Additionally, the CV profiles of the subsequent cycles are nearly overlapping (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a), illustrating the superior cycling stability of the 3DSC-700 electrode.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/medium/am9b14366_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0004.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) CV profiles of 3DSC-700 at 0.1 mV/s, (b) discharge–charge profiles of 3DSC-700 at 100 mA/g, (c) cycling stability of 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700 at 5000 mA/g, (d) rate performance of 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700, and (e) Nyquist plots of the 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700 electrodes.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b14366&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">There are two apparent sloping platforms at ∼1.25 and ∼1.75 V during the charge/discharge processes of the 3DSC-700 electrode except for the initial cycle (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b), which is ascribed to Na<sup>+</sup> insertion into the 3DSC-700 structure to react with covalent sulfur and consistent with the CV curves. The 3DSC-700 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b), MDC-700 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4b</a>), and SC-700 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5b</a>) present initial charge/discharge capacities of 526.1/1087.7, 58.7/227.1, and 282.1/686.3 mAh/g, respectively. Cycling stabilities of the prepared 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700 were tested at different current densities. When tested at 100 mA/g, after 100 cycles, the 3DSC-700 can retain a reversible capacity of ∼ 450 mAh/g, but the capacities of MDC-700 and SC-700 after 100 cycles are 36.4 and 216.9 mAh/g, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>). Even at 5000 mA/g, the 3DSC-700 electrode still possesses outstanding extra-long cycling stability (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>c) and presents a highly reversible capacity of 225 mAh/g after 3000 cycles. Rate performances of the 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700 electrodes are tested at 1000, 2000, 3000, 4000, and 5000 mA/g. Reversible capacities of 343.6, 307.2, 287.4, 275.1, and 264.6 mAh/g are reached respectively for the 3DSC-700 electrode at each current density (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>d). Notably, when the current density decreases to 1000 mA/g, the capacity can be restored to 354.9 mAh/g, illustrating that the 3DSC-700 electrode has a high ability to endure high current changes. Additionally, compared to 8/SC-700 and 67/SC-700, the 3DSC-700 electrode also exhibits higher capacities (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>). <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S2</a> lists the comparison of electrochemical performance between the 3DSC-700 electrode and those reported in the literature, where the 3DSC-700 presents the highest capacity among the reported carbon-based material for SIBs whether tested at low or high current density. To explore the impressive high-rate performance of the 3DSC-700 electrode, EIS was adopted to study the electrical conductivities of the electrodes. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>e displays Nyquist plots of the 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700 electrodes. As shown, all of the three plots consist of a semicircle and an inclined straight line. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref47 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 34, 47 and 48">(34,47,48)</a> The semicircle relates to the double-layer capacitance, the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>), and the electrolyte and electrode resistance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref47'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref47" aria-label="reference 34 and 47">(34,47)</a> The straight line arises from the Warburg impedance (<i>Z</i><sub>w</sub>) and corresponds to the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in electrodes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48" aria-label="reference 48">(48)</a> The <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values of the 3DSC-700, MDC-700, and SC-700 electrodes are 215, 965, and 628 Ω, respectively. The lower <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value of the 3DSC-700 electrode is attributed to the co-effects of sulfur doping, the special structure, and metal particle decoration.</div><div class="NLM_p">Pseudocapacitive contributions, Na adsorption energies, theoretical capacities, and Na diffusion energy barriers were further adopted to investigate the excellent high-rate performance of the 3DSC-700 electrode. CV profiles at different scan rates are tested, and the results are displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>a. All relevant calculation equations are presented in the <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>. The calculated b values of peak1 and peak2 are 0.84 and 0.96, respectively. These results manifest that the performance of sodium storage in the 3DSC-700 electrode is related to both diffusion-controlled reaction and surface capacitive-controlled behavior. The 3DSC-700 electrode delivers a capacitive contribution of 88% at 0.6 mV/s (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>b). Moreover, the pseudocapacitive contributions are 81, 85, 88, 89, and 90% at 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1.0 mV/s for the 3DSC-700 electrode, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c). These results exhibit that the capacitive contribution is augmented gradually with the increasing sweep rate. The capacitive contribution in the 3DSC-700 electrode is higher than 80%, illustrating fast reaction kinetics characteristics in it. That may explain why the 3DSC-700 electrode has outstanding capacities at high current densities.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/medium/am9b14366_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0005.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) CV curves and relationship between log <i>i</i> and log ν plots (inset) of the 3DSC-700 electrode at different scan rates; (b) diffusion contribution and capacitive contribution at 0.6 mV/s; (c) diffusion and capacitive contributions at 0.2–1 mV/s; top and side views of the most stable Na adsorption configurations for (d) pristine and (e) S-doped carbon. (f) Na adsorption energies of pristine and S-doped carbon of Na atoms. (g) Na diffusion energy barriers and pathways of pristine and S-doped carbon.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b14366&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Density functional theory (DFT) calculations are performed to provide an in-depth understanding of S-doping effects on the performance of SIBs, including Na adsorption energies, theoretical capacities, and Na diffusion energy barriers, which determine the charge/discharge rate of SIBs. Detailed DFT calculation methods are shown in the <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/suppl_file/am9b14366_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>. A fundamental precondition of SIB anode materials is that the material must have a relatively strong Na adsorption ability. For pristine carbon, sodium atoms prefer to be adsorbed on the hollow site with an adsorption energy of −1.23 eV (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>d). After incorporating S atoms, the most stable sites are the top of S atoms with an enhanced adsorption energy of −1.62 eV in comparison with pristine carbon (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>e). This is attributed to the fact that the higher electron density surrounding the S atoms is in favor of the adsorption of positively charged Na atoms, endowing the S-doped carbon with improved Na adsorption ability. Then, we examined the maximum Na adsorption capacity by increasing the number of sodium atoms. The adsorption energies gradually decrease upon increasing the number of sodium atoms (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>f), which can be attributed to the increased repulsive electrostatic interactions between Na atoms. As a consequence, pristine and S-doped carbon can accommodate at most four and six Na atoms, corresponding to the chemical formulae Na<sub>4</sub>C<sub>16</sub> and Na<sub>6</sub>S<sub>2</sub>C<sub>14</sub>, respectively. The mobility of Na atoms is another important factor for anode materials, which is closely relevant to the charge and discharge rates in SIBs. Therefore, with the aid of the NEB method, diffusion pathways between two nearest-neighboring adsorption sites for Na are examined (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>g). It is found that Na diffusion on S-doped carbon is faster than that on pristine carbon due to the lower diffusion energy barrier (0.29 and 0.20 eV for pristine and S-doped carbon, respectively), indicative of a faster charge/discharge rate in S-doped carbon. In combination with these superior characteristics, including enhanced Na adsorption energy, higher Na storage capacity, lower Na diffusion barrier, and higher electronic conductivity, it can be concluded that the S-doping, the special neuronlike 3D network structure, and metal particle decoration play vital roles in improving carbon-based anodes for Na-ion batteries.</div><div class="NLM_p">The intriguing cycling stability and excellent rate performance of the 3DSC-700 encouraged us to explore its actual performance in sodium-ion full cells. In a Na-ion full cell, the 3DSC-700 anode is coupled with a homemade NVP cathode. The typical CV curves of the Na-ion full cell in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a show that there are two apparent cathodic peaks at around 2.5 and 3.65 V during the first cathode scanning process and one wide oxidation peak around 3.1 V during the first anode scanning process. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>b shows the discharge/charge curves of an NVP//3DSC-700 cell at 100 mA/g. There are two apparent sloping platforms at ∼3.4 and ∼3.65 V in the charge/discharge processes, which are relevant to the deinsertion and insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> and consistent with the CV curves. The full cell exhibits charge/discharge capacities of 342.14/273.32 mAh/g in the first cycle (based on anode mass). Moreover, the full cell delivers good cycling performance and a high capacity of 229.64 mAh/g could still be obtained after 50 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>c). The inset images in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>c show that the blue light-emitting diodes (LEDs) can be driven by one assembled cell. These results demonstrate that the 3DSC-700 has a promising application as an anode in commercial SIBs.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/medium/am9b14366_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0006.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. (a) CV profiles of a Na-ion full battery tested at 0.1 mV/s. (b) charge/discharge profiles and (c) cycling performance of the Na-ion full battery at 100 mA/g (inset image in (c) shows the LEDs illuminated by the full battery).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b14366/asset/images/large/am9b14366_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b14366&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i11">Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In conclusion, ZIF-8/ZIF-67-derived dodecahedrons and Th are employed as fulcrums and the sulfur source to synthesize a unique neuronlike 3D network structure S-doped carbon. Due to the co-effects of the special neuronlike 3D structure, sulfur doping, and metal particle decoration, the 3DSC-700 electrode delivers outstanding capacity and extra-long-term cycling stability when it was used as an anode in SIBs. Moreover, theoretical calculations certify that the S-doping can endow the carbon-based material with enhanced Na adsorption energies, more Na atom accommodation, and a lower diffusion energy barrier. This work also indicates the promising potential of MOFs and polymer used in energy storage fields. Our work may open up a new avenue to solve the problems of both lower rate performance and poor cycling stability of carbon as anodes for practical SIBs.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div University of Technology (Shandong Academy of Sciences), Jinan 250353, P. R. China</span></div></li><li><div class="authorItemInformation"><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor strong">Mei Li</span> - <span class="hlFld-Affiliation affiliation">School

                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrical energy storage for transportation-approaching the limits of, and going beyond, lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thackeray, Michael M.; Wolverton, Christopher; Isaacs, Eric D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7854-7863</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The escalating and unpredictable cost of oil, the concn. of major oil resources in the hands of a few politically sensitive nations, and the long-term impact of CO2 emissions on global climate constitute a major challenge for the 21st century.  They also constitute a major incentive to harness alternative sources of energy and means of vehicle propulsion.  Today's lithium-ion batteries, although suitable for small-scale devices, do not yet have sufficient energy or life for use in vehicles that would match the performance of internal combustion vehicles.  Energy densities 2 and 5 times greater are required to meet the performance goals of a future generation of plug-in hybrid-elec. vehicles (PHEVs) with a 40-80 mi all-elec. range, and all-elec. vehicles (EVs) with a 300-400 mi range, resp.  Major advances have been made in lithium-battery technol. over the past two decades by the discovery of new materials and designs through intuitive approaches, exptl. and predictive reasoning, and meticulous control of surface structures and chem. reactions.  Further improvements in energy d. of factors of two to three may yet be achievable for current day lithium-ion systems; factors of five or more may be possible for lithium-oxygen systems, ultimately leading to our ability to confine extremely high potential energy in a small vol. without compromising safety, but only if daunting technol. barriers can be overcome.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrM-qA7OWNUGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgLWCMWhRuiSg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XptVWku70%253D&amp;md5=d681fdb77cf76bcc104bd3726dabddb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201100691"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">White, R.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hollow carbon nanospheres with superior rate capability for sodium-based batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Kun; Fu, Lijun; White, Robin J.; Yu, Linghui; Titirici, Maria-Magdalena; Antonietti, Markus; Maier, Joachim</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This study examd. the electrochem. performance of hollow carbon nanospheres as anode material for sodium ion batteries.  The nanospheres were prepd. by a facile, sustainable hydrothermal procedure.  Findings revealed the excellent cycling stability and rate capability of the nanospheres when used as anode materials for the sodium-based batteries.  Mass transport and storage were effectively enhanced through addnl. refinement of material parameters, including morphol. and size, resulting in a considerable improvement of the electrochem. performance both for lithium and sodium.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpFHFn_p5w7jrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgLWCMWhRuiSg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtVOrtLbF&amp;md5=24c5da0ec94442593a692757cb3a0c66</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201803260"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ke, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Defect-Rich Soft Carbon Porous Nanosheets for Fast and High-Capacity Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Adv.
